C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	This is what I can decipher from the provided Old French text. I have translated it line-by-line into modern English as accurately as possible while maintaining the context and meaning of the original:

de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sick

de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the loins

de la tentigene	of the tentacle
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentacle is a separated part on the natural body, so it is too ugly to see; and some women also have it like a hand, and this is the cure for it. You should burn the excess of the tentacle with your hand or fingers gently; do not cut it too much, that if it comes off, you can then cure it with other cures until it is healthy again; and at another place, which comes out of the mouth of the mare (a female animal), take it and use it, and perhaps it will jump away, and it resembles a cow's head, and for this reason they called it the old "cow disease". If you want to cut it, do as we have said about the tentacle, and cure it until it is healthy.
de erratique	de erratique

des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the woman
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Various types of abscesses can occur in the woman's groin area, including syphilis, infectious abscesses, herpes, and fistulas, as well as hemorrhoids and apothecmia (a condition causing painful swelling). In the treatment of a groin abscess, it is important to first understand its nature. If the patient experiences sharp pain and fever, and the abscess turns red, consult an expert. Do not hurry to cut it open, but rather wait until the pain subsides; then position the patient comfortably with their legs spread apart and their feet elevated. Place a small pillow under their thigh and support their back. Have the patient sit up and lean forward, supporting themselves with their arms. Then, using a suitable instrument, insert it into the mouth of the woman, taking care to avoid causing any harm. If the instrument is large, cover its tip with a cloth to protect the woman's throat. Once inserted, take the measure of the depth of the abscess, ensuring that the instrument does not cause any further harm. If the abscess has opened, cover it with a wet poultice made from oil or boiled roots, placed directly on top of the abscess and the opposite leg. Apply a dry poultice to the leg opposite the abscess, keeping it clean and free of debris. After 2-3 days of application, remove the poultices and apply a mild ointment. Repeat this process for several days until the abscess has healed. It is important not to raise the affected leg using a clamping device or by holding it up with a cloth; instead, use a pillow or cushion to support it comfortably. Additionally, avoid using hot water or applying hot herbs directly to the affected area. If there is swelling in the groin area, apply cold compresses to reduce the inflammation. Finally, if the patient experiences a severe fever or their condition does not improve with rest and poultices, seek medical advice promptly.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth

Mestier is the first skill in midwifery that she knows the natural figure of childbirth, and the signs if you see the woman rush down, and desires to smell the air: then the baby's foot comes out; then you know that these births are according to nature, and the issue is with her head, and the second one with her; and when you see these signs, you lightly press her belly so that the baby comes soon; for when he descends on her head, if it is the second with him, and it is well-washed, then the husband is free of his excesses by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally. For it comes no fewer times on its feet, and comes on its neck or shoulders, or hands, or comes on its belly, or sometimes, and is transformed by accident on her throat, and by other evil figures; thus it is important for midwifery to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how she must help him.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the cure of wounds; now we will tell you about the cures for hands and medicine, according to achievement.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and because of this they are made.

ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	Here is the translation of the text line by line:

Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen

Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second type of stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you join together the leather and the fabric with a needle and strong thread;

ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is for a man;

Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Or I will tell you the nine proper ways to stitch:

quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	How she has received the cure of right by right, if you have pricked the head of the shoulder or the cost or where you have pushed the needle

Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of sewing, which Galens explains properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is so that if it is so that there is no seam, which joins the .ij. parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the main joints to the other main joint in this way:

as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as .ij. shoulders of the syringe

Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	And Galien says thus of that word, and no one testifies to it,

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as it is with other wounds:

Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of any other medicine in most cases when the wounds are simple;

Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is torn.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is due to the vegetation of the veins and the subtility of the entire body, and the approach of its nature to that of children.

de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil

Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If this pain is felt in the intestines, and does not cause any trouble for the patient,

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or that she is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	know that any wound or abscess, once it has healed, is called a "fistula" in its entirety.
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when it has been cut and sewed up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And the fistula is according to the green nut, hard and white, or there is no pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also called a crow's feather.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	ne either jump clear bow, and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	ne ever poke, and sometimes enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no cure,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is no more than from one of the .viiij. causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	this is to say, by small amount of blood or pussy;
ou por sa malice;	or for his malice;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because it has hard skin and on the lips, so that it does not grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	Where there is too much bow
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	Where the leg is sore, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	Where the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Where, because of corruption, there is a risk of pestilence;

et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have listed all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that you know the cure for fistula which is done by hand work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	I see that a fistula can occur in all limbs of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	Because there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the physician, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spine of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet;

et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see a clear fistula with your own eyes, take an iron or brass ring, and if the fistula is straight, try it on;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, so the search for a thin tent of punch,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the punch folds up under the tortuosity;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula is very twisted and you cannot well search for it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then the cautery by one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For moisture is very short from one breach to another, and purifies.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	Then inspect it with your hand, so that you can know if there are bones or nerves, and is completely shaved.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	And ask the patient to feel for pain when you press with your hand, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	And when you know for sure the location, and whether it is far from a joint, a nerve, an artery, or a vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu'il laisse les poilz tant qu'il soient lons et igals; et s'il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu'il ne se muevent tant qu'il naissent.

tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine corrodes the surplus that is retained at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put a paste of olive oil and honey, until it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy by this, then the fire cautery as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the nose is corrupted by the fistula, then the patch.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or main member is hurt, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the nose is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if the king is removed until the whole bone is corrupted,

si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means of doing this by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone that has become rotten, and you can pull it out with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	If it is extracted with .i. an appropriate instrument for this,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is only one bone, and the treetops are not broken, do not leave any of them;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes it difficult, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If it is broken and moist, and the rain and snow are severe, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something that will cause pus on the wound.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it until the pus has grown around the bone,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then, if the bones will come loose more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh bone;
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	If you are able to understand only a little corruption until the blackening is complete, then
puis restoure la plaie;	Then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is much corruption and there is only a little left of the bone,
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it can be sewed and covered up to where the corruption ends, and then treated until it is solid;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula which happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man aged 18-21 years who had a pain in his leg due to an internal cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as matter came out of his leg, and there was a large abscess, and he had no clear cause to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the mirror due to madness goes up so high that it covers the abscess.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and corroding matter, and became an ulcer, and I came out of a perforation that completely discharged bowels and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many mirrors were cured within .ij. years, and I had no skill in the art of medicine,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called, and I saw a leg and the medicines that were used to cure it,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and he who runs through small openings causes great damage to the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the youth's body turned red, and had an orange color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came together with the other on both sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I therefore hastened and struck upon one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it rotted and eaten away, and the decay went down to the bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what appeared to me to be a rotted bone, and I cared that there should be no other decay, except for that which I had discovered;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long period of time, and could not bind it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	I found continued decay in the bone and sawed it, and then I held it, and bent over to weld the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but as soon as I had put my hand on a palm of the bone, I broke it entirely off,
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and he was healed and welded together firmly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and so we shall not say more about this work except for its weakness in the disease which cannot be borne.

Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For with blood loss there was often, but he was completely healed, and
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and it gave birth in place of the bone a hard mass, and was of good disposition and had no harm or opposite from all, nor did it cause any harm or come to harm.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if his jaw is broken in any place of the neck, it should be done thus:

dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may be dislocated due to heat or due to cold;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicine that this corrosion by the remedy of medicines, and it does not benefit at all,

Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the cap comes to the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;

Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Now let the wound in the liver be opened and left as it is, and delay it as much as possible so that it does not cause a great gathering of bowels.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the finger nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	is a finger nail that grows out of the palm of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when he is dressed, and no care is taken, so that he comes to an abscess at the cheek,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and cut and dig so that they reach the root of the nail, and sometimes cut it all.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes the corrosion up to the bone, as much as there is a pungent pain, and has the head of the two sides, and the color runs.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	if you cut off all the excess that has been retained by the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The fire cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound, and the nail is sound.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the skin, and begins to prick, and bleeds,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so that you put a relief on the nail that pricks the skin, and stops the bleeding,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and pour it up high, and gently and lightly pour this thin liquid,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put upon the remnant of the wound burning and corrosive remedies to prevent anything from being left.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the remedy with garlic as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then grind it and apply it firmly, for as long as the bone is腐ったままであれば、それは治ることはないでしょう。
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	And if you see the corruption of the two, then grind it with us as it is in front said,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and treat him until he is well;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is fierce and bruised, and it hurts greatly, then you must first heal him.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the nail with a twist of the spatulum from above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not come too close to the nail bed, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if so, let something be placed on top of it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sore on the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The following is the translation:
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance it has or it has bones, and never has knuckles,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in neither of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those who are born at either end do not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those who are born at the joint of the two may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of that which is chubby so is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut off at the root a large spudicum.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint should be treated carefully: if you keep him warm.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In those who are born or must be cut at the derriere, it is necessary that you first chop the hair around the anus down to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then chop the bone with a suitable scissor, and then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations come from two things: either they occur by nature at birth, or by injury to the joint, or by burning with fire, or by similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you understand that you should fix this dislocation according to its natural form;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	and then place between two tents or drapes moistened with oil so that it does not stick;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or place between two thin pieces of linen, until the joints are fixed, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the hands join together with the palms, then hold them like this.
Des vils	Of the vile things
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Are vile, large, wrapped, full of superfluous melancholy, which come from many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more come in legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, that to others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you do not let him take any more purges, and then heal him of the bazillica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure for iron is to be done according to three methods: one is with coprolites, and to draw out the black blood forcibly;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another method is if you can feel the vein, and draw it all out forcefully.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size of the scar is according to this method: raise the first leg of the patient with very hot water, until the large vein is visible, then
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then pull out the leg of the patient from behind the thigh just up to the part above the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in .i. place, or in .ij., or in .iij., with a large-sized blade;
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then, with your hand, draw out and squeeze the black blood from one hand to the other, as much as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then, dip it in; command that he eats meat mixed with black coarser;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and the swelling when the veins are empty, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The healing method for this is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is hair on it,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and dry it. raise the leg with hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it on the fire, and then put the joint in the right place at the foot of the leg, or in the part between the ankle and the knee;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then wet the skin with vinegar, and scar the vein from each side, until it is felt when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it turns red and black, and when it enters or leaves the skin so seems to us as a white string;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then pour the blood out, until it is lifted up from the skin, and then put it on the skin lightly,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut the blood out with a knife, twice; then scar the skin over the vein until it is felt,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	and then return it to its place, as you have done, and hold it with one hook, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then make another hole, or as many as you need, then bring the wire up, and attach it to the foot of the bone,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then thread it through, and tie it at each hole, until it has passed all the way through, then cut it off;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it through, so take a strong double-threaded needle;
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and the leather and the tray, and I pour on it. i.e.,
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from spilling, for if it spills, we cannot extract or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished treating it, put wet wool soaked in wine and oil over the wound; and heal it until it is well.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	and if it is twisted and bent together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If it is necessary for you to split it cruelly, but do not cover it; and train it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that covers the viscera if it is curved, and does not cut, so that it covers the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curve, for if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but if it were thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein:
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance does not grow anywhere else than in the legs, and this comes from a rash that causes the skin to fall off,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If it creeps in from within the body and coils up, dislodge it between the skin and the shell.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if there is a sign of the onset of this vein that it comes in the leg, there is a great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limbs change place, and the vein begins to flow outward like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When you open the head, if you wrap a piece of cloth around it from one third to two thirds, and then tie it up,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth hanging down from the leg, and every time that there is a point where it comes away, if the wrap around the cloth, and the bandage,
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, if you take a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cover all of it up again, until it is completely wrapped up;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you make it, it enters the cart, and brings an abscess and putrefaction where, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this thing, it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the head, and there remains nothing or a core;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is never this vein when it is treated with long palms, or with
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and I have had ten honourable men come to me, who was of long palms, and when you make it, if it is a small bottle or a big one, and pierce it until the end,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all is well; and the matter within, which is useless, is removed to its place, and medicines are brought against putrefaction each day, then heal it as you do abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And no hand is applied to this vein, and even less when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out with blood, and how it bleeds; then heal it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that come between the skin and the hair
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "buff disease" because it often affects buffalo.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between leather and cart, and goes through the whole body rising and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and feels well at the touch of skin or fur, and jumps about.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with pus, as it comes towards and winds and worms and parasites enter into it;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt about his evil, for when he goes through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes to the oil,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	may enter again and destroy the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him cure and draw it out, if one can only go so far:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so that it may lie on top of a strong cord, tightly tied.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	and then cut up and down, and let his back be put into perfect shape in the chair, and you do not believe it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery is applied to him, until he dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, if it is corrected oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see coming near the head of the oil, hold the soul with a fire; then cut up, and let his back be put into perfect shape in the chair;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the sick person of the change of cors of soluble medicines for the bad humors porries,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and wash with meat that is rotten porridge.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and so moves from member to member; and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then, I saw it grow bigger like a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	much faster than anything else, and like quicksilver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little later it corrupted throughout the whole body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that she was twisting together in her chest, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how she moved her member from member, for I have never seen such a disease in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	All the same, I wish many things well, but well wish pain from him to another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not wish this, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was why the woman's chest was tight and her veins were visible;
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason the wind appears constricted;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and does not agree with these who are greedy, and have moist hearts and opened veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the leg is raised and kept in position, and then copious sweat comes out at the root with a forced movement towards the outside;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the leg; and if you do not see it in your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the healer of those who treat wind with pills, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Are different, according to their appearance and according to the places of their flight in the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is such that there are some with great tips, and small, and curly, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have .ij. angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those where there are parts;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which shite in no member so shite according to .ij. ways: or in a principal member shite,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as the brain, liver, pancreas, kidney, lungs, intestine, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	For when it shite in any of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you hereafter, it reveals:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary for you to extract this arrow, for death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when the bad sign does not manifest itself to you, and the arrow is not perfectly extracted, if it breaks, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces and splits the bone, and the medicine that is above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a cut and bruise and swelling and redness around the wound, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and difficulty in speaking, and vomiting of food.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is without nose or ears; and by chance loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the moist scar that looks like pus, and also as if it were burning with fire;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign will appear to you, if you keep the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not stuck.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	the sign of the arrow when it hits or falls, is that it is near the left breast, and also as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance it becomes mute as well as birds, and a dark short breath, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	surcharged with doubt that death will come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that nocks is that without a plain of foam jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he sighs loudly and cries for cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces through the back, there is a great deal of pain and crying out; and all the members move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow goes into the stomach, so that none of the meat is indigestible.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters the abdomen and does not go through the intestine, so there is no hope for cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters the bladder and the urine does not flow, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, if the face and the nose and the throat and the shoulder and the arm and the back and the hand and the leg and the limb are saved according to many provisions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the lung or artery, and it does not come out, so that I tell you what happened to me, because otherwise you would do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to me that an arrow got stuck in my chest or armpit at the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to extract it, and I pulled it from another side by the fat of the ear, and I was healed without any noise.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I extracted an arrow that got stuck in the oilfat of an ear by pulling it from a piece of paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was inserted, and I could not achieve anything beyond the tip towards the wind
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was very large of a blue color, lighter than an ear; the shot was sound, and no bad accidents happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I shot an arrow at a Christian's throat, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew the barbs, and I hid them so that I shot, and the Christians were sound.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And tie an arrow to his bow, which was on his back or stomach, and I thought he was dead.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then it had passed xxx days, if it did not improve its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow string, and tied it, and threw it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a bow with an arrow nocked, and it is the wound that is sewed up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and hold back the arrow inside it, and do not prevent its natural movements,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor find harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man, to whom he shot an arrow into his face, and it was sewn into the wound;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and held back so as not to suffer great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And put an arrow at the king of the prince's house, who had a bad back pain,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was a little leaning to the right side; and the arrow was all lodged
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been wounded for three days. I found the wound very tight and narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I treated it with a subtle remedy, and did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a piercing pain and pain in his left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the leech-infested plaster for digestion, lest the leeches inflame it;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I felt the leeches of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster to his hands every day, and resolved the wound quickly, and delayed the patient's death for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he felt the arrow .i. day after his birth; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied to the wound a corrosive aqueous medicine every day, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tested it, and felt the tip of the arrow which hardened at its base;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	and I adjusted by the opening of the wound by that medicinal water until the head of the arrow was visibly seen;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and I kept well the terms for .iiij. months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I opened the wound so that I could take hold of the nails, and spread them from one side to the other, and could not pull them out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to study and devise tools, until I took it with nails well made,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what I have written in this chapter, until now I have been doing so, and have restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and sewed up the wound, and healed the patient entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or have I told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you place your remedy on what I do not say, for the books can not take all;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare only a few things, and on those that are present and failing;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	try nine operations, and nine instruments, for the dismemberment of foreign things which come in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are members or they are fixed except for three ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d'autre part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which leaps forward through a gap, is an arrow entering flesh, and does not leap forward at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leap forward, then leave it as the fleshrot is corrupted inside, and the arrow's flight is obstructed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in a bone, and cannot come out, then leave it for a certain number of days, and every day move it.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, so pierces everywhere. i.e. through the thin skin, until the inner part is widened, and then treat.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes down one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said may happen to the patient: if you do not treat it, but leave it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if an arrow enters just up to the sinuses, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not lodged far enough in the bone, it does not go any further than medicine.
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient sometimes remains for a few days without any bad accident, if the device to pull.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is deeply lodged and cannot come out, if you administer tar treacle as I told you; then cure the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	and if the arrow is in place in the heart so that we cannot see it, if we seek it with all our strength; then
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if you do not use any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by stretching the wound and by the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the hurt is great when the wound is made.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and stretch the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If the bone is broken in two parts by the blow that you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or twist the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but rather pull it out with more pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out at once, if the arrow remains stuck, then twist it, because extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the blood flowing out is contrary to what we have said in regard to the remedy in his chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting into the nerve and the vein, and put not yourself in danger of extracting the arrow.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or soon or late, or firmly or gently; and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow came out.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot do that, then follow the sign which the stars show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where it opens nothing of its own, or the skin is swollen in a certain place if you see or feel apart:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then on, as long as the nail can take it, and then remove it: but do not cut now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round, as long as it goes into the bone and widens it, and then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for a while, and then begin the extraction again as long as it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if an arrow is embedded in him, then he pierces it to the very tip.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if an arrow has lodged in him, then you should remove it with a scalpel, for it is a sharp instrument.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the handle of the instrument; and then pierce it through,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if an arrow is pierced, then you should pierce the instrument with the point entering in, for joy of the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then you must cut all around where the poison is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	and then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow enters into the chest or the belly or the bladder or the side, and it is close to an organ, and you can cover it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and do not cover the vein or nerve, and then extract the arrow, and then treat the wound, if it is necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the forceps used to treat splinters are like an owl's beak, and thus have this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do it: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the splinter.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the blade is also like an owl's feather,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To bring the tip of the arrow, as it is here described:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pliers to bring and to hold, because such is this form:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the neck common

Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The patient should be kept warm and quiet.

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the health of the face in ancient diseases, and migraine, and jaundice;

Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	All the same, it is not appropriate that the flames are too fierce; and the healthy one across, for the bone is close, and by chance the flames break when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healthy one of the two veins that are in the two arms should be used for cauterizing, and with oil for tinea, and with red spots, and with the ringworm, and with the oil disease of the face;

et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not make it too long a cautery, and make the blood run according to your need, then let it rest for a night, for it is soon healed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The following is the translation of the provided text from Old French to English:

De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Of the healing of the limbs above the lips, and corruption of the gums, and splits in the lips, and lumps and swellings in the mouth.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to have the sick person sit before you, and hold his neck as I said;

et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and rub the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and over the foot goes much rain;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Heal the ankle, or the foot, or the leg, as it may be needed.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, so that you don't go down, and heal it crossing as well as you can; and let the flame burn out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if they cannot come out, put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you heal it the first time, start the second above a little hole, because the leech is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerve, if as we have said, and so do with the foot of the other stone evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the leg are at the ankle and their blood flows to the pain in the thigh when it is caused by a wound.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this blood is that the patient should enter or exit, removing it from the ankle .iii. two in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so let the blood flow in all ways that you can, and crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is necessary for you to cut it, for its roots are strong, and it grows very quickly on many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, neither rain from the roots opens or closes the foot, and towards the small toe, and keep away from the nails;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make it run so that you see blood, and then loosen the ligature, and put cotton on it and hold it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	For sucking wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and the ventosity is done in this way: either by cutting and pulling out with pain, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosity, which is done without cutting, in this way: either it is all fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and the ventosity which is done by cutting and pulling out blood, made in this way: of the horse's neck,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is entirely at the top of the head; and the other is halfway down the throat;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and .ij. others on .ij. coasts of the neck; and the suction cup is removed from the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction cup is removed from the shoulders; and the suction cup is placed on the scalp;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction cups are removed from the arms; and the suction cups are removed from the legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups are removed from the ankles; and the suction cup treatment for blood should not be done on large veins that are spread out over the body, but only on small ones that are close together;
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this do not be afraid of any pain, as it is done when opening a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be dressed, nor burned, nor stung in any disease that comes from excess, as long as all the body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, because of the necessity of illness or out of habit, we dress it every hour during the month, or at the end, and eat it and drink it in each ten days;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to vomit, do so even if it is not necessary; if they have eaten too much;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if they have red spots and pain in their face, and in their forehead, and around the throat, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and feel pain.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if they are blind and deaf, and feel pain and strange things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and especially when it is mid-moon, we order them to breathe after. iij hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The medicine of the muscle due to the greasiness of the head ... that comes to the hair, and it does not come that it is after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this vaporization if it is in the place of the medicine of the cerebral,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it does not come that it is of cold complexions in use, or who has chaff, for this makes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and it does not come that it is of those who have cold head illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become confused, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little further down due to the confusion of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suctioning should be done at the base of the skull and at the back of the skull, and for this reason it is used to extract the bone.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and at the opening of the channel of the pemoon, and all around, and with repetition;

Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventsations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,

And is in the place of the health of the basilica; and it comes that you command to the doctor that he express his hand to put on, that he does not cut the artery, and does not bring damage from blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventsations of the mouth si vaut to disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the place of the health of the 2 lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventsations of the shoulders si valent to disease that comes from heat and filling up. Li ventosations des poilz du costel valont a maladie que vient par la mouillesse, et par le frottement, et par l’asseclement, et par la moellure, et par la corruption.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds of the neck should be as strong as those of the upper arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instructs the surgeon to not cut too deep, for the limb is naked of skin, and knows how to cut nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the neck, which is at the base of the spine, should be made large and deep, and the surgeon must be careful not to cut too deeply, for it may hit the spinal cord and cause great damage; and if it were to slip, it would make large wounds and cause much pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Legs' suction cups if they are opened up, because they draw blood from all over the body, and they are akin to the old pains of the knees, and of the ankles, and of the bladder, and they put flowers in motion; and they are in the realm of the .ij. sophenes, and of the .ij. feet, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring about premature death in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The mode of applying the suction cups is that you should place them first empty, and suck them promptly, and then fix them firmly, and move them evenly, and do not cease from doing so until you see the red and inflamed spot, and perceive the pain of the blood; then remove them, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some whose flesh is tender, and their pores clear: so it is necessary to wound them once only, and to make deep wounds, and a hole through them; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the flesh is thick, then it is necessary to wound it two times: the first time to make a small hole in the thick flesh of the groin.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the flesh is very thick, then it is necessary to wound it a third time; and when we want to suck blood little by little, we suffocate it a little at a time.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to stop the bleeding, let us start often; and if the blood is thick, so do not be too quick, and the end is that the cuts should be felt immediately.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover those who have thick and tough skin and who have been pricked, that you moisten the spots with oil that opens and dissolves:

But it is necessary to wash after the ventilation with pink water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or other thing.

et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is worth that he warm himself, when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned;

si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary for him to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in the shade, and similar things;

et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some people three times or more musk before and after ventilation to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be subtle the drink, but it is not necessary that who are hot they drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed to hurt are those that are placed on the liver, and the tongue, and the podagra, and on the belly and the bowels and the rain and the hinch, for this member does not suffer to be hurt on the skin,
